  9. Bottom line: A novel twist on a shaver: a cooling bar that does feel cool against your face. But, while this has the customary excellent Braun build quality and ergonomics, it falls short when it comes to closeness and can even be a bit harsh.<br /><br />Full review: I'm a big Braun fan - have their 3, 5 and 7 series. I also have razors from pretty much every manufacturer, but a Braun Series 7 is my all-time favorite. This Braun brings a couple of interesting features to bear, but doesn't come close (pun sort of intended) to unseating the Series 7 or, for that matter, any other Braun I have.<br /><br />I like shavers, so this is a long review. Sorry - you can jump to the end if you just want the conclusion.<br /><br />Build quality<br />Excellent. This is made in Germany, and it feels solid and substantial. The shape is comfortable to hold securely with wet or dry hands due to the inclusion of non-slip pads on key grip points. It's plastic, as expected, but avoids the cheap feel that you can get with some razors (including the Braun Series 3). Hold this in hand, and the first word that comes to mind is \\"solid.\\" The only place where the build quality is less than perfect is the bottom end, with noticeable seams in the plastic.<br /><br />It comes with a stand that is nicely made. I like that it makes a soft audible beep when the razor is properly positioned for charging. Note that the stand MUST be used for charging - the plug goes into only the stand, and can't be directly connected to the razor. Something to keep in mind if you plan on using this on an extended trip - you have to take the stand along if you want to charge it.<br /><br />Ergonomics<br />Excellent. Easy to grip and there's a thumb pad that it perfectly positioned. My only quibble is that the bottom of the razor is angled a bit too much. I would have preferred a more rounded, softer design approach. But, that's just a matter of taste rather than function. The ergonmics of the stand are also excellent since you don't have to position it just so -- just plop it in, and it seats.<br /><br />Motor sound<br />Not great - more on the tinny side than I expected. Granted this is again an aesthetic issue, but I found the sound of the motor to be more annoying than other Brauns, and not what I was expecting.<br /><br />Shave quality: face<br />Decent, but not spectacular. It takes multiple passes to get it as close to what I can get with a Series 7 in just a pass or two. It gets there, but it does take longer. It also pulls at the hairs far more than any other Braun I've used. Not \\"ouch\\" bad, but the pulling can be felt.<br /><br />Shave quality: jawline<br />Again, decent. I did get some minor irritation, but it got my face smooth.<br /><br />Shave quality: neck<br />Not good. Despite multiple passes, it could not get as close as a Series 7 nor a Series 5. More significantly, it did irritate my skin after these multiple passes. That's the first time I've had a Braun redden my skin.<br /><br />Trimmer:<br />Excellent. Love the push-up trimmer format (same as the 3 and 5 series) rather than the flip-out as found on the 7. Works well and easy to use.<br /><br />Cooling:<br />It does work. I did feel a coolness from the aluminum bar, but did it help with the shave? Not for me. Fun and interesting, but adds little to the end result. It also drains the battery far more than just shaving. The feature can be turned on or off with a button on the front.<br /><br />Wet shave:<br />This can be used as a wet shaver, but Braun is inconsistent as to what that means. On their web site, they say that \\"...it is important that you do not use any shaving foams, gels or lotions which may act as a thermal insulator, and are not compatible with the alcohol based cleaning solution (and may potentially also damage the device).\\" But, at the same time, they say you can use the razor in the shower. I guess when they say \\"wet shave\\" they mean water only.<br /><br />I tried it with water and it didn't add any benefits to the shave quality. For real wet shaving (with actual shave gel) I much prefer my Series 3.<br /><br />Cleaning<br />I do not have the model with the cleaning station, nor do I think it is needed for this design. While I love the cleaning station for my 5 and 7, the head design on this is super simple to clean under running water. Braun recommends oiling the heads once a week if you manually clean it. I've found using Remington Shaver Saver spray (or the analogous product from Norelco) works very well for lubrication, plus it has a nice scent.<br /><br />Conclusion<br />My three stars may seem to be a harsh rating. But when I look at the price of this compared with the 3, 5 and 7 Braun series, I was expecting something that performs nearly as well as a 7. This does not. It compares most closely with a 3 series in terms of shave quality and comfort, but lacks the true wet shave capabilities as some 3 series models have, plus it's more irritating on the neck areas.<br /><br />Yes, the build quality is excellent and the cooling bar is a novel addition, but for the price, this falls short and I can't give it more than a 3 star recommendation.'t add any benefits to the shave quality. For real wet shaving (with actual shave gel) I much prefer my Series 3.<br /><br />Cleaning<br />I do not have the model with the cleaning station, nor do I think it is needed for this design. While I love the cleaning station for my 5 and 7, the head design on this is super simple to clean under running water. Braun recommends oiling the heads once a week if you manually clean it. I've found using Remington Shaver Saver spray (or the analogous product from Norelco) works very well for lubrication, plus it has a nice scent.<br /><br />Conclusion<br />My three stars may seem to be a harsh rating. But when I look at the price of this compared with the 3, 5 and 7 Braun series, I was expecting something that performs nearly as well as a 7. This does not. It compares most closely with a 3 series in terms of shave quality and comfort, but lacks the true wet shave capabilities as some 3 series models have, plus it's more irritating on the neck areas.<br /><br />Yes, the build quality is excellent and the cooling bar is a novel addition, but for the price, this falls short and I can't give it more than a 3 star recommendation.

  16. I've been very fortunate to try out a new shaver from Braun. They selected me to test out their newest shaver and give my opinions.<br /><br />First, it's a bit of a departure for them in the technology. Having been a Braun fan for many years, I've followed their advances and seen them focusing on moving heads and cleaning systems to get a closer and cleaner shave. This model does not pivot, rather the head remains fixed. And there is no cleaning regimen involved, a simple brush is included, harkening back to older models of Braun shavers.<br /><br />What has not changed is the quality manufacturing and good shave. It's a rather substanital unit to hold in your hand. It has an ergonomic grip that fits and feels comfortable in the hand. Rubber is placed in all the right places, so at the bathroom counter, it won't slip or fall easily. I did not find the lack of a pivoting head a detriment at all (was the pivoting head really all that necessary or did they figure out a flexible head that really works now?). The contours of my face were navigated nicely and I got a close comfortable shave.<br /><br />The big add though to this shaver is the cooling sensation that (in theory) is to make for less razor burn and less irritation. I'm fortunate to not experience too much rough shaving consequences, so I am not one to easily address that. But what I can speak to is how cool the sensation is and how it really does make for a pleasant shaving experience. The cooling action is optional. The user does have to depress a clearly maked button in the palm portion of the shaver to activate the cooling. Once this is done, a metal bar in the shaving head cools very quickly so that on each stroke of the shave a cold surface glides across the face. I found it to be a rather pleasant experience. There was definitely no razor burn and my face was comfortable at the end of my shave.<br /><br />As usual for an electric shaver, the cut is not as close as a blade can get, but it does a great job of cleaning up my face without all the prep and clean up as well as not requiring lots of creams, lotions, or similar. I simply turned on the shaver, ran it across my face as necessary and then used my regular daily moisturizer and I was good to go. I am a big fan of the shaver, I will use it on days I just can't take the time to use a blade (my wife really does like the closer shave) or for some of the trickier parts of my face where running over and over to get the desired results can rough up my face. The shaver does have a pop up trimmer which I found helpful in evening my sideburns, so that is a good feature to like as well. In the box is the shaver itself, a cradle for charging, a cord to connect to a power source and a small brush for cleaning the debris in the shave head. So, it's a bit of a departure, but if you are Braun fan, you know the quality of construction and shave you will get. If you are not a Braun user yet - this might be a good time to join the fanclub. Braun indicates this appliance has an expected life span of 7 years. I won't be able to review that until November of 2020. But if that is close to right, the cost seems well worth it compared to what you'd pay for blades and associated products.

I suppose if I were shaving for a few minutes and the unit started to become warm from friction, this would be welcome, but usually by the time that starts to happen, I'm finished. So it's neither here nor there for me. The recharging base doesn't have a firm latch so it's easy to put the unit in such that the two metal contacts in the rear of the razor don't touch the recharging contacts. I suppose that's why Braun added a &#34;beep&#34; sound to let you know that the contacts are touching appropriately and the unit is charging. I'd prefer that the contacts be redesigned so that they work every time. So overall, an interesting effort, but I prefer my 7680.

  32. This review of the Braun Cool Tec Men's Solo Shaver is from a former Norelco shaver fan. Braun won me over in 2010 with their [[ASIN:B003YJAZZE Braun Series 7-760cc Pulsonic Shaver System, Black and Silver]]. I found that the Braun series 7-790cc Pulsonic shaver system offered me a noticeably superior shave to any Norelco shaver that I had used previously.<br /><br />The primary advantage of the Cool Tec Men's Solo Shaver, as touted by Braun, is its cool shave option. (More on this in a moment.) The shaver also feels quite solid and firm in the hand. Although made primarily of plastic, there is some heft to the shaver. It simply feels heavy and that's a good thing in my book. I also prefer the sideburn and mustache trimmer to the one on the Braun series 7-790cc Pulsonic. It operates in a different flip out manner makes it easier to hold and use.<br /><br />The shaver uses Braun's cooling technology they they refer to by the moniker of \\"Cool Tec\\". Braun claims that \\"Cool Tec\\" \\"effectively cools down the skin while shaving, delivering a pleasant and skin-friendly shave without negative impact on shaving results.\\" Braun states that it does this without using gels or lotions to improve the shaving process. That sounds quite nice, but I wondered if the performance of the shaver's engineering matched the hype of its marking folks.<br /><br />To check reality verses marking hype, I tried using the shaver both ways. (You can decide whether or not to turn on the \\"Cool Tec\\" function on a shave-by-shave basis, so if you don't like it you don't have to use it.) My sense was that switching on the 'CoolTec\\" feature did give a somewhat more comfortable shave. Whether the cooling effect will deteriorate over time, I don't know. It's too early to tell. However, for now, you can definitely feel the cooling--so score one for engineering on this shaver.<br /><br />Another nice feature is a travel lock. It is engaged by pressing the on/off switch for three seconds. The same action alsodisengages the lock. (It's a toggle on, toggle off function.) A lock symbol in the display indicates whether or not the travel lock is engaged. This is extremely handy for those unhappy times when your shaver switched itself on in your travel bag. Of course, that always occurs when you leave the charger at home. Everyone knows that you get plenty of shave time from a fully charged battery--so why bother carrying the extra weight of the charger?<br /><br />The accessories that came with the Braun Cool Tec Men's Solo Shaver were a mixed bag. The instructions promised that a carry pouch was included. It wasn't. The instructions also recommend that the shaver heads be oiled once a week with a light machine oil. A good idea that almost nobody does because very few people keep a bottle of machine oil in their bathrooms. Braun thoughtfully included a small bottle of light machine oil with the shaver. A nice touch that was not clearly mentioned as being included in the box by the instructions. It's so much better when the instructions always match the item.<br /><br />There are two holders that can be used to hold the shaver when not in use. There is a charging shell and shell power socket (base) that is included with the shaver. There is also an optional \\"Clean&Charge\\" station that serves as a base. The included two-piece shell and base is flimsy and doesn't seem to provide the stability that a shaver this heavy deserves. Furthermore, I was disappointed that the cleaner base that is used for the series 7-790cc Pulsonic shaver system was much too narrow to hold the Cool Tec Men's Solo Shaver. Why Braun can't have one cleaner base that serves all their shavers is beyond me.<br /><br />Despite some of my nit picks, I suspect that the Cool Tec Men's Solo Shaver will quickly become my favorite shaver. It's heft in my hand, travel lock and cool shave feel put it miles above any other shaver that I have used. Well done Braun!<br /><br />*** Update ***<br /><br />Several other reviewers have noted that Cool Tec Men's Solo Shaver does a poor job shaving the neck. Having used this shaver for several weeks now, I can say that this is true. This is a disappointing aspect of an otherwise decent shaver.

Unfortunately, you can't plug your Cool Tec directly into a wall outlet with the charging cable if your shaver's charge is low, but the charging process is fast. I still have a Braun wet/dry shaver from 8 years ago that still charges in minutes and holds a charge, so I'm assuming this won't be a problem with my Cool Tec. I also think Braun is trying to avoid users from plugging their Cool Tec into wall outlets and foolishly taking a plugged-in shaver into the shower.<br /><br />Of course, the main draw for this shaver is active cooling technology. I thought the Cool Tec feature was gimmicky at first, but it does provide a refreshing, cooling sensation on your face while shaving. You don't have to use the cooling function-it's activated by the light-up blue button in the middle of the shaver.   105. I always wait a little while after using something before giving a review, but I've been using the Cool Tec shaver for about 3 weeks now (I got the shaver through a program run by Braun), and I think I can accurately identify the positives and negatives of the razor.<br /><br />Positives - It's hard to identify what benefit, exactly, the cooling strip has, but it feels nice as immediate cooling when you're shaving. It's hard to explain, but I feel like it is helping my skin (even if I can't define why). The trimmer on the back also does an admirable job of defining edge lines, although I've only used it to set the line at the bottom of my side burns - the divider between hair and shaving area. Also, it is rather easy to clean, which is an extra little time-saver.<br /><br />As for the razor itself, it does a great job of trimming hair on the first or second pass, especially on everything above the neck. As I have sensitive skin, this is important to me, because (and this is a problem I've had in the past) multiple passes over the same area tends to aggravate the skin. The dual-foil setup of the razor helps with the contours on my face. On everything below the neck (and this is detailed in the negatives), the razor did a good job of getting hair that grows in the direction that it is supposed to. It did a good job going over the jaw line, which I've previously found to be a problem with foil razors.<br /><br />Negatives - If you're traveling, using the cooling strip tends to burn the battery a little quicker than one would like. I found that I could get by a 3-day trip without having to recharge, but any more than that, and I'd need the charged as well (which isn't that large or difficult to travel with, just an extra thing to bring), I actually checked the manual on this, and it tells you the same (the razor kills the battery much more quickly with the cool strip on), but I enjoy the cool strip enough that I use it all the time.<br /><br />Also, and this may just bethe way that I hold the razor, I find that I frequently bump the button for the cooling strip, constantly turning it on and off. That's probably just the way I hold the razor.<br /><br />The other negative with this product is the same I've had with all foil razors - if your hair (especially on your neck) doesn't all go in the same direction, you need multiple passes over the same area to get the hair in the direction in which it grows. I don't want to blame this particular product for it, more so the style of product, but this one did not offer any improvement over the other foil razors I've used.<br /><br />All in all, I enjoy this razor, and am continuing to use it (despite having to make an extra couple of passes on the 'trouble' spots on my neck). The cooling sensation plus the easy cleaning makes it worthwhile.

  142. OUT OF THE BOX<br /><br />Out of the box you've got the shaver, two pieces of plastic that form the charging stand, and the power cord. Other than the instruction manual, there isn't much else in the box. The first step is to simply attach the plastic parts together so you can charge the shaver. The power cord plugs directly into the stand so the shaver can rest in there and charge via the metal contacts. This is the only way to charge the shaver, it must be in the dock. That can be somewhat inconvenient if used for extended trips.<br /><br />THE SHAVER<br /><br />The saver itself is basically a mid-range foil shaver in terms of features and functionality. It's a tad bulky and on the heavy side for most shavers in this class. It has 2 separate foils that are spaced apart due to the middle \\"cooling bar\\" and cutting system. The shaver is straight as can be, no angle or adjustments. The foils of course move up and down for some movement, but it is limited in this regard.<br /><br />There is a power button and of course, the blue snow-flake to enable cooling functionality. At the back you have a basic trimmer. It opens upward into a locked position allowing for forward and backward movement, without closing. Although the blades are very short and actually angle backwards, which can limit it's usefulness. There is no cleaning system with this unit, but the foil pops off making cleaning about as easy as it gets for this type of razor.<br /><br />THE SHAVE<br /><br />I started my shave without washing my face and at 90 degree angles, as directed. They've made it very clear you shouldn't wash your fast before the shave as I suspect it can prevent a smooth shave. And the 90 degree angle would be required since the head doesn't move and is stuck in one position. I started without the cooling function on one side and it went as expected. Then switched on the cooling for the other side. First, that cooling bar gets rather cool very quickly. It basically feels like a cold metalbar going across your face. It's a rather odd sensation at first. My infrared thermometer was indicating around 68 degrees.<br /><br />Unfortunately, as is expected with most mid-range shavers, they just don't do quite as good of a job as the higher-end models. Essentially requiring more passes over the same area that others went through much easier. Despite this, once I was done, I couldn't help but notice there was slightly less irritation, as my skin can be somewhat sensitive. And at the end of the shave, my face is smooth as can be.<br /><br />PROS<br /><br />+ Cooling bar actually works<br />+ Dual foil system<br />+ Water proof<br />+ Lockable trimmer<br />+ Li-Ion Battery<br />+ Easy to manually clean<br />+ Dock for easy charging<br />+ Smooth shave!<br /><br />CONS<br /><br />- Not cheap<br />- No head adjustment<br />- Somewhat Bulky & Heavy<br />- Can't charge without dock<br />- Short, limited trimmer blades<br /><br />CONCLUSION<br /><br />I should note that my most recent shavers are the Braun 790 and Panasonic ES-LV81-K shavers. While these are much more expensive units, I am of course taking into consideration the price and functionality compared to other shavers I've used in the past. I've been using electric shavers decades, so I've gone through a few. With all that considered, and despite my skepticism, I did find the cooling technology to actually work. I'm quite happy with the shave, which says a lot considering it's competition. If you have a good shaver, I don't think it's awesome enough to buy a new one. But if you're looking to upgrade and are interested in trying something just a little different, I consider this one recommended.

  181. I've been a fan of Braun electric shavers for several generations of their products. Having very sensitive skin, I've experimented with every type of blade, cream, oil and machine possible. I finally found the right combination of double edge safety razor blade, handle and cream that leaves me unscathed in getting a perfect shave, but since I travel for a living and razor blades are frowned on by the TSA and scary men with uniforms and hand cuffs, my preferred solution was an effective electric shaver, especially while traveling. Braun has been the most effective alternative for me with the last previous incarnation being their Series 7, 790 shaver, which I've used with complete satisfaction. Admittedly, though, it's effectiveness came at a cost of being just slightly aggressive, and if I pressed to hard against my skin in a hurry to get out the door, I managed to inflict some irritation. This new series of shavers from Braun , boasting a cooling bar, in all honesty had the ring of a gimmick after perhaps having nowhere to go to improve an already near perfect product as their 790. I'm very happy to admit that I was cynically mistaken. this shaver, while not perfect, is welcome and appreciated.<br /><br />My first reaction when examining it was frankly, disappointment. It looked and felt like a cost cutting compromise. Unlike the 790, the shaving head is fixed and doesn't pivot. It shed the beautiful glass indicator at the bottom that graphically showed both the degree of charge and the degree of hygiene, i.e. when it was time to thoroughly clean the head. The 790 had a clever arrangement where the sideburn trimmer rose vertically out in a 90 degree snap that made it very accessible, whereas this new model has an arrangement where the trimmer lamely slides up with less drama and range. I was ready to pronounce it a disappointing cost reduction design at a premium price. Until I fired it up and tried it. It has a solid, monolithic feel, and requires more conscious maneauvering due to the lack of the pivoting head I was accustomed to. But that translated into feeling less gimmicky and more solid. The shave and cutting action does seem less aggressive than my old Braun which also seemed disappointing, until I realized that it was in reality more gentile to my skin. But the whole point to this new incarnation is The Cool factor. There's an aluminum bar positioned between the two cutting foils that presses against the skin and it is indeed cool. I cynically muttered that, while it had a refreshing sensation, that it wasn't making any difference to the skin. Again, I gratefully had to assess that I was wrong. Evidently, that quick touch of coolness is enough to calm any abrasiveness the blades and cutting foil might cause. I think I did have to revisit a spot or two because of the more mild aggressiveness, but ultimately the shave was complete and effective with no irritation whatsoever. Even the shape of the shaver which is mildly more of a broader &#34;Y&#34; and is bulkier at the top than the the older model is more ergonomic and so more natural to hold. I should note that according to the manual, using the Cooling feature does diminish the battery charge more quickly, whatever technology that cooling involves, so you can press the blue button on the front to disaffect the cooling. But since the shaver is recharged as soon as you place it back in the stand and since the cooling factor is really the whole point of this thing, I'm not sure why you'd want to turn that off. In some ways, the look and design does appear to be pared back and no doubt is cost cutting on the manufacturing, the reality is that it seems to be achieving a superior end result. Which is the whole reason you choose an electric razor and this particular Cooling design to begin with. If you, like me, are migrating from the Braun 7 series, it will take a small adjustment. But especially if you have sensitive skin prone to irritation, you should find this model awelcome and effective product. It might be mentioned that it's made in Germany, which gives me more confidence in it's integrity than if it had been stamped out in China. I've only used it a few days but from that limited exposure, at this point, I can highly recommend it and don't think you'll be disappointed.welcome and effective product. It might be mentioned that it's made in Germany, which gives me more confidence in it's integrity than if it had been stamped out in China. I've only used it a few days but from that limited exposure, at this point, I can highly recommend it and don't think you'll be disappointed.

  191. While I received this product via a program run by Braun, the opinions here are entirely my own.<br /><br />The Solo comes with a charging shell, base that can hold it the shaver upright, wall charger, a small amount of machine oil, small cleaning brush, a vented clear plastic cover to protect the foil blades and of course the shaver itself.<br /><br />This shaver is a little heavier than I thought it would be so it takes a little getting used. As soon as you get a good feel for it, it's not that noticeable. The top portion has a textured, rubber grip area and the finger indentation and trimmer areas are made of rubber, so it doesn't get too slippery. Although, for some reason, they used the same slick plastic as the charging shell and base for the front part on the sides and very bottom which doesn't make any sense to me. It would be much better if it was all rubberized or at least had a more matte plastic for that portion.<br /><br />Speaking of the plastic quality, I think that the base that keeps the charging shell upright feels a little cheap. The plastic used is not thick and stable enough when you consider this is not an inexpensive shaver. With the somewhat heavy shaver sitting on it, it can wobble and just doesn't feel sturdy at all, so I'd say it's best not to use it.<br /><br />It's pretty easy to charge. You just lay the back of the shaver on the 2 metal pins of the charging shell (which is a light, but thankfully semi-firm plastic) and plug the charging cord into the shaver before plugging it into the wall. The on/off button will blink green until it is done charging and it takes a good hour to fully charge. It would be nice if we could just charge without this extra piece, though. The wall charger does have a convenient spiral cord which I love, but it's made of very cheap plastic, so it may not last that long.<br /><br />The cooling feature (which is indicated by a snowflake) really does work but sometimes I find that I hit the button because of the placement, turning it off. I suppose I still need to get used to that part but perhaps if it was smaller, that would be very helpful. But this feature has really helped my skin because other shavers would sometimes give me harsh irritation and redness. The cooling sensation is hard to explain but it really makes my skin feel refreshed and I only use aftershave about once a week now.<br /><br />As for the trimmer, it's easy to press the small button to slide it out and is a good size for most, I think, at a drop under an inch wide. It might be nice if it slid out 1/4 - 1/2 inch more only because it ends up being just a tad higher than the blades, so you have to be mindful of that.<br /><br />When cleaning, I've found that rinsing it under hot water with a gentle liquid soap while it's on works great. Sometimes I remove the foil blade cartridge, which is very easy, and gently tap or use the included brush to clean the remaining hair from inside, just be careful that you don't touch the \\"SensoBlades\\" because that could damage them. I've been using a drop of the supplied machine oil every so often to keep the blades at their best.<br /><br />The travel lock function is excellent so that it doesn't go off by accident. When pressed, the shaver turns on for a few seconds and then a lock symbol appears and you're good to go. Also, when not in use, the vented clear plastic cover does an okay job but doesn't stay on very well if it's moved around, so it's probably best to buy a carry bag to keep it in better condition.<br /><br />Overall, this is a very nice shaver and does what it says. The cooling feature, while some may say it's a gimmick, does what it is meant to do. It's possible all skin types may not benefit but it's worth a try. One thing to note, though, is that using this feature does considerably shorten the charge of the shaver. I would recommend this if you are looking for a comfortable shave, but it's disappointing that many of the accessories aren't better constructed since the shaver itself feels very solid.
